its aim if it provide the basis for future discussion it originate in the experience of its five writer at the summer school for working-class student hold in connection with the worker ' educational great democratic tradition be bring face to face for the first time with they full ultimate responsibility as british citizen upon the way in which that responsibility be realize and discharge depend the future of the democratic principle not only in these island but throughout the world democracy be not a mere form of government it do not depend on ballot box or franchise law or any constitutional machinery these be but its trappings democracy be a spirit and a atmosphere and its essence be trust in the moral instinct of the people a tyrant be not a democrat for he believe in government by force neither be a demagogue a democrat for he believe in government by flattery a democratic country be a country where the government have confidence in the people and the people in the government and in itself and where all be unite in the faith that the cause of they country be not a mere matter of individual or national self-interest but be in harmony with the great moral force which rule the destiny of mankind no form of government be so feeble as a democracy without faith but a democracy arm with faith be not merely strong : it be invincible for its cause will live on in defeat and disaster in the breast of every one of its citizen belgium be a living testimony to that great truth british democracy have carry this principle of confidence to the furthest possible point alone among the state of europe great britain rely for she existence and for the maintenance of she world-wide responsibility upon the free choice of she citizen she privilege be extend to all : she active obligation be force upon none trusting in the principle of individual freedom and upon the sound instinct and understanding of she people she leave it to each citizen to make he choice whether and in what manner he shall serve he country never have responsibility so arduous and so urgent be lay upon the citizen of any community : and never have the citizen be so free to choose or to decline the burden the world will judge great britain and judge democracy accord to the measure of we free response what be the nature of the responsibility cast upon we at this crisis it be threefold it concern the present the past and the future there be three question which every citizen must need ask and try to answer for himself the first and most urgent be a matter of present decision : what be my duty here and now the second involve a judgment of past event : why be it that we be at war be we fight in a just cause the third involve a estimate of the future and of the part which british influence in the cause of human progress and for the welfare of the people involve in the war it be with the second and especially with the third of these responsibility that this volume be concern sixty-two year ago reaction reign supreme in europe after the great national and social uprising of 1848 and england look on passively while the hope of freedom be crush in bohemia hungary and italy mazzinus the noblest of italian patriot the most prophetic soul among nineteenth-century nationalist select this moment of profound despair to publish a essay entitle _ europe its condition and prospects _ which burn with the passion of a inextinguishable faith pierce the veil of the future and foreshadow in a almost miraculous fashion the situation which face europe and england to-day nothing print in this country since the war break out express more clearly the real issue of the mighty conflict and the part we country be call to play in it than the follow word in reference to the unredeemed people of europe utter by the great italian more than half a century ago : they struggle they still struggle for country and liberty for a word inscribe upon a banner proclaim to the world that they also live think love and labor for the benefit of all they speak the same language they bear about they the impress of consanguinity they kneel beside the same tomb they glory in the same tradition and they demand to associate freely without obstacle without foreign domination in order to elaborate and express they idea to contribute they stone also to the great pyramid of history it be something moral which they be seek and this moral something be in fact even politically speak the most important question in the present state of thing it be the organization of the european task in principle nationality ought to be to humanity that which division of labor be in a workshop -- the recognize symbol of association the assertion of the individuality of a human group call by its geographical position its tradition and its language to fulfill a special function in the european work of civilisation the map of europe have to be re-made this be the key to the present movement herein lie its initiative before act the instrument for action must be organise before build the ground must be one 's own the social idea can not be realize under any form whatsoever before this reorganisation of europe be effect before the people be free to interrogate themselves to express they vocation and to assure its accomplishment by a alliance capable of substitute itself for the absolute league which now reign supreme if england persist in maintain a neutral passive selfish part she will have to expiate it a european transformation be inevitable when it shall take place when the struggle shall burst forth at twenty place at once when the old combat between fact and right be decide the people will remember that england stand by a inert immovable sceptical witness of they suffering and effort the nation must rouse herself and shake off the torpor of she government she must learn that we have arrive at one of those supreme moment in which one world be destroy and another be to be create in which for the sake of other and for she own it be necessary to adopt a new policy england to-day have adopt this new policy she have respond to mazzini 's appeal by step european development the political structure of the continent have oscillate this way and that accord as these idea have in turn assume ascendancy over man 's mind and when as in 1848 both claim attention at the same time the whole edifice be shake to its very foundation in england on the other hand it be the social idea alone which have be a motive force in the nineteenth century although she have always have to reckon with the national idea across the st george 's channel owe to she fortunate geographical situation she acquire national unity many century ago and have always be able to defend it successfully against the danger of external aggression the national idea therefore have long cease to be a aspiration and consequently a revolutionary force among we it have be realize in actual fact we have grow as accustomed to it and as unconscious of it as of the air we breathe thus englishmen as they attitude towards ireland have show find it difficult to understand exactly what the principle of nationality mean to those who have never possess national freedom or be in constant danger of lose it this be perhaps especially true of the english work class who grow to the full stature of political consciousness some fifty year after the last serious threat to we national existence be make by napoleon and upon whom the burden of the social idea press with peculiar weight and yet unless the significance of the principle of nationality and the part which it have play in the history of modern europe be realize it be impossible to enter fully into the true meaning of the present tremendous conflict what then be nationality the question be more difficult to answer than appear at first sight a nationality be not quite the same thing as a nation for example there be a german nation rule by the kaiser wilhelm ii but this do not include twelve million people of german nationality who be the subject of the emperor of austrium or again there be the swiss nation which be make up of no less than three distinct nationality still less be the term state and nationality synonymous for if they be then the native of indium might claim to be of the same nationality as ourselves or _ vice versa _ the united state would be regard as part of the british empire because a large proportion of they inhabitant happen to be of british descent the word race bring we somewhat nearer to the point but even this will not satisfy we when we remember that the slavonic race for example consist of a large number of nationality such as the russian the pole the czech the serb the montenegrin etc or that the english -lrb- as distinguish from the other three nation of the unite kingdom -rrb- belong to the same teutonic race as the german nevertheless a belief whether well ground or not in a common racial origin be one of the root principle of the idea of nationality what be a nation the great magyar nationalist kossuth ask a serb representative at the hungarian diet of 1848 the reply be : a race which possess its own language custom and culture and enough self-consciousness to preserve they a nation must also have its own government object kossuth we do not go so far explain he interlocutor one nation can live under several different government and again several nation can form a single state -lrb- 1 -rrb- both the magyar and the serb wear right though the latter be speak of nationality and the former of nation the conversation be in fact instructive in more way than one it would be difficult to find a better definition of _ nationality _ than that give by the serb speaker a common language a common culture and common custom : these be the outward and visible sign which make a people conscious of its common race which make it in other word a nationality -lrb- footnote 1 : rw seton-watson _ the southern slav question _ p 46 -rrb- the element of consciousness be all-important there be for example member of the finnish race scatter all over northern russium but they evince no consciousness of any kind that they be ally to the nationality which inhabit the country of finland again it be only within recent year that the serb and the croat in the the realisation of this fact have spread from the study to the market-place we see the formation of a new nationality that of the serbo-croat the research of historian and other learn man have do a immense deal to stimulate the development of nationality during the past century but they be unable of themselves to create they the fact of kinship be not enough community of language custom and culture be not even enough to be a real nationality a people must be conscious of all these thing and not merely conscious but sufficiently conscious to preserve they and if need be to die for they now the interesting thing for we about a nationality be that it be always strive to become a _ nation _ a nation as we have see may be compose of several nationality but such case be rare and be due to peculiar geographical condition as for example in switzerland and great britain or to external pressure as in belgium which have as it be weld together the different racial element into a single whole in general therefore a nation be simply a nationality which have acquire self-government it be nationality _ plus _ state ireland a nation the warcry of the irish nationalist party be a claim not a statement of fact ireland will become a nation when its desire for self-government be satisfy the case be instructive because it show that it be not necessary for a nationality to become a _ sovereign _ state in order to be in the full sense of the word a nation it be perfectly possible as we serb remark for several nation to form a single sovereign state but as a general rule all such nation will be allow to manage they own internal affair the self-governing dominion of the british empire and the magyar of hungary be nation though they be subordinate to they respective imperial government in question of peace and war treaty obligation etc the real test of national existence be ultimately a sentimental one do the nationality inhabit a give country regard the government under which it live as a true expression of its peculiar genius and will do the state of which it form a part exist by its consent or have it be impose upon it by some alien authority or nationality be it a territorial unity or have it be split up into section by artificial frontier all these question must be answer before we can say of any nationality that it be also a nation the national idea therefore which have be one of the chief factor in modern history be essentially a idea of development its root be the conception of nationality that be of a people consciously unite by race language and culture and from this spring the larger conception of nationhood that be of a nationality possess its own political institution govern by its own consent and co-extensive with its natural boundary as we shall see later political development do not always stop at the nation-state further growth however be extra-national in character it may either take the parasitical form of one nation impose its will and its culture upon other nation or it may assume the proportion of that highest type of polity yet know to mankind a commonwealth of nation freely associate together within the confines of a single sovereign state -lrb- 1 -rrb- -lrb- footnote 1 : see chapter ix for further treatment of this -rrb- § 2 _ the birth of nationalism : poland and the french revolution _ -- with these general type _ -- let we now turn to italy a country which have in the past be as much of a european tom tiddler 's ground as belgium though for rather different reason italy be inhabit by a race speak a find very useful in deal with the national idea in other country § 6 _ the national idea in germany : a case of arrest development _ -lrb- 1 -rrb- -- nothing for example could be more instructive both as a study in nationalism and as a aid to the understanding of the present situation in europe than a comparison between the making of modern italy and the making of modern germany at first sight the german empire with its marvellous progress its vast resource and its world-wide ambition would appear to be a even more successful example of national development than the kingdom of italy its demand for a place in the sun its hustle diplomacy its military spirit its obvious intention to expand territorially if not in europe itself then in asia or africa be all take as symptom of this success no doubt there be a certain amount of truth in this view the truculence of german foreign policy be to be partly attribute to that form of swollen self-consciousness and self-complacency to which all nation be subject more or less and which be most likely one would suppose to be find in country where a nationality have recently succeed in make itself into a nation the natural instinct to regard one 's own nation as the peculiar people of god and to look down on other nation as lesser breed without the law be a phenomenon which must be constantly reckon with in any comprehensive treatment of nationalism every nation have its own variety of it in england it be jingoism in france chauvinism in italy irredentism in russium pan-slavism and so on these be instance of over-development of the national idea due either to some confusion between race and nationality or to simple national megalomania which usually subside after a healthy humiliation such as we suffer in england for example in the boer war or as russium suffer in she struggle with the japanese -lrb- footnote 1 : the student be advise to read the chapter on germany before begin this section -rrb- yet a careful examination of the german body-politic will reveal symptom unlike those to be find in any other nation german nationalism be over-developed in one direction because it be under-developed and imperfect in other direction apply we three test to the german nation and it will be find to fail in they all national boundary and state frontier do not coincide because there be still some twelve million german live outside germany in austria-hungary -lrb- 1 -rrb- germany be a state but not a unitary state for she still retain the obsolete particularism of the eighteenth century with its petty prince and dynastic frontier and lastly the government of germany can not claim to express the general will while more than a third of the voter in the empire be swear to overthrow the whole system at the earliest opportunity the german nation in fact be suffer from some form of arrest development and arrest development as the criminologist tell we be almost invariably accompany by morbid psychology that germany at the present moment and for some time past have be the victim of a morbid state of mind few impartial observer will deny it have however not be so generally recognize that this disease -- for it be nothing less -- be due not to any national depravity but to constitutional and structural defect which be themselves the result of a unfortunate series of historical accident let we look a little closer into this matter consider the three defect in german nationalism one by one and use the story of italy as a aid to we investigation -lrb- footnote 1 : there be also german live in switzerland the baltic province of russium and the united state of america but these may be regard as lose to the german nation as the french canadian be lose to france -rrb- first then why be it that while the unification of italy lead to the inclusion of the whole italian nationality within the state frontier with the trifling exception above refer to the unification of germany be only bring about or even make possible by the _ exclusion _ of a large section of the nationality germany like italy be hamper by tradition inherit from the mediaeval roman empire represent by a ancient capital which stand in the path of unity why be it that while italy could not and would not do without rome germany be compel to surrender vienna and to exclude austria the answer be : because the unification of germany be only possible through the instrumentality of prussium which would not brook the rivalry of austrium and therefore the latter have to go the problem of the making of germany as it present itself to the mind of bismarck be first of all a problem as to which should be _ supreme _ in germany prussium or austrium in other word bismarck care more for the aggrandisement of prussium than for the unity of germany -lrb- 1 -rrb- to the mind of cavor the problem of the unification of italy present itself in a totally different light for he there be no question of the aggrandisement of piedmont though he no doubt feel pride in the thought that the house of savoy be to possess the throne of italy austrium be expel from italy in 1860 not that piedmont might take she place as ruler of liberation in 1859-60 in the first place the austrian be not foreigner but german whom it be necessary for reason of state not of nationality to place outside the rest of germany germany have in fact to choose between national unity and state unity and she choose the latter partly because prussium really decide the matter for she partly because she realize that the establishment of a strong german state be the essential prelude to the creation of a strong united nation austrium have to be shut out in 1866 in order that she might be receive back again at some later date on germany 's own term in the second place austrium be in no sense the oppressor of germany as she have be of italy she be simply the preside member of the german confederation who as the rival of prussium as the inheritor of growth and development of the german state it be now time to turn from the german state to the german people § 2 _ the real germany _ -- the difficulty of establish german unity have lie in the fact world-problem can make the concert of europe a reality such be the general attitude of mind among the german public of the younger generation let we now turn to the effect of this new outlook upon the _ note _ -- such consider german writings as have come to hand since the outbreak of the war show little tendency to cope with the real fact of the situation or even to seek to understand they they seem to indicate two development in german opinion -lrb- 1 -rrb- a great consolidation of german national unity -lrb- except of course in poland and alsace-lorraine -rrb- -lrb- 2 -rrb- a tendency to forgo the consideration of the immediate issue and to hark back in think to 1870 or even to the war of liberation it be difficult to judge of a nation in arm from the writings of its stay-at-home but no one can read recent article by the leader of german thought without feeling that the german be still before all thing and incurably the people of poet and philosopher and that by a tragic irony it be the best and most characteristic quality of the race which be sustain and will continue to sustain it in the conflict in which its dream have involve it chapter iv austria-hungary and the southern 1902 -rrb- in April 1909 a week after the international crisis evoke by austrium 's annexation of bosnium have come to a end i pay my first visit to cetinje the tiny mountain-capital of montenegro and of bosnium upon a reluctant europe but instead of follow up this success by a determine effort to solve the southern slav question on a austrian basis she allow the confusion to grow yearly worse 9 _ the future of the southern slav _ -- there have always be two fatal obstacle to a austrian solution of the southern slav problem -- magyar hegemony and the dual system to which alone that hegemony together be to call into existence a huge administrative machine and he see equally clearly that if such a machine be not itself to become a disruptive force through the personal ambition and self-aggrandisement of its member it must be frame on democratic and not aristocratic principle as mr maurice bare put it peter the great introduce the democratic idea that service be everything rank nothing he have it proclaim to the whole gentry that any gentleman in any circumstance whatsoever and to whatever family he belong should salute and yield place to any officer the gentleman serve as a private soldier and become a officer but a private soldier who do not belong to the nobility and who attain the rank of a commission officer become _ ipso facto _ a member of the hereditary nobility in the civil service he introduce the same democratic system he divide it into three section : military civil and court every section be divide into fourteen rank or _ chin _ the attainment of the eighth class confer the privilege of hereditary nobility even though those who receive it might have be of the humblest origin he hereby replace the aristocratic hierarchy of pedigree by a democratic hierachy of service promotion be make solely accord to service lineage count for nothing there be no social difference however wide which could not be level by means of state service this be partly what be mean when it be state in the last paragraph that russium be socially the most democratic of modern country the system establish by peter the great exist to-day russium be govern not by a feudal nobility like that which grind the face of the poor in france before the revolution of 1789 nor by a number of capitalist who live by exploit the worker for neither feudal nobility nor capitalism -lrb- as yet -rrb- have any real power in russium she be govern by a civil service and by a civil service more democratic than we own where the higher post be as a rule only open to member of the upper and middle class less exclusive than that of indium where the higher official be nearly all recruit from the member of a alien race -- a civil service in short whose only close parallel be the hierarchy of the roman catholic church imagine the roman church as a secular institution with a monarch at its head ruling by hereditary right instead of a elect president like the pope and you get a very fair idea of the russian government machine all that we associate with the word aristocracy in the west the hereditary principle primo-geniture the accumulation of the land and capital of and when he meet a nobleman he meet he on term of spiritual equality while acknowledge he superior position in the social scale a twin-brother of english snobbery be english hypocrisy this as have be well say be a kind of social cement for it be a tribute to a standard of social conduct set up by the dominant class in a nation and since there exist no dominant class in russium but only a dominant hierarchy draw from all class hypocrisy be absent from the russian character mr stephen graham who be i believe at one time a clerk in a london office find we civilisation so intolerable that one day good-will such open hospitality such a instinctive respect for personal liberty -- liberty of thought and of manners -- such tolerance for the frailty of human nature such a abundance of what the great russian novelist dostoieffsky call all-humanness and st paul call charity as in russium all this of course do not come about as a result of the bureaucratic system it spring like that system itself from the fundamentally democratic spirit of the russian people § 2 _ religion _ -- the last paragraph will read strangely to those people whose only idea about russium be glean from newspaper time to say something of the revolutionary movement of 1905 and of its ruthless suppression which give russium so evil a reputation in the eye of western europe it be my good fortune to be a resident truth but as what one man of limited experience and vision conceive to be the truth about the russian revolution the main reason why english people get mistaken idea about russium be that they imagine russian to be nothing but englishman picturesquely disguise in fur and top-boot and because they interpret the political situation in russium in term of english history and politics as i have already try to show russian be build differently from english people _ from the soul outwards _ while the political and social condition of the russian empire be totally unlike anything that have ever exist in this country if therefore the real cause of the movement of 1905 and of its failure be to be rightly understand we must put away from we mind the desire to find analogy in the english revolution of 1642 and 1688 or the french revolution of 1789 or the social revolution of which karl marx dream russium can only be interpret in term of russian history and russian condition in one thing however the russian revolution be like all revolution which have ever be or be ever likely to be viz that it be concern with two distinct issue one a narrow question of political and constitutional reform and the other a far wider question involve a attempt to reconstruct not merely the institution of society but also to transform the ideal and conception upon which society rest let we first of all consider the narrower political issue this be simple enough the outbreak of 1905 have as its primary object the set up of some form of representative government which would control the bureaucratic machine it have be already point out that the constitution of modern russium be largely due to the genius of peter the great during the nineteenth century however it become apparent to think russian that the constitution for the sake both of stability and efficiency need development in the direction of popular representation the plea of efficiency be really far the stronger of the two have peter the great be eternal he might possibly have continue to exercise a effective control over the administrative system which he create for he be a man of superhuman energy and will-power but most tsar who be man of ordinary capacity find it impossible to do so the consequence be that the bureaucracy acquire what amount in practice to absolute irresponsibility now irresponsibility be demoralise to any administration however democratic be the principle upon which its official be select a bureaucracy ruling without proper external control become a prey to the demon of red tape routine officialdom and place-hunting it tend to stifle individual initiative and the sense of moral responsibility since it forget the real object of its existence -- the good government of the country -- in its passion for self-preservation and its desire to secure the smooth-working of the machine it become inhuman intensely conservative and corrupt above all it develop a hyper-sensitiveness to lay criticism which compel it to do all in its power -- and in russium that power be unlimited -- to crush freedom of speech and freedom of the press the problem however of devise some popular check upon its action be a extremely difficult one for the simple reason that the mass of the russian people never have take and even to-day do not take any interest in political question nevertheless the tsar alexander ii who be one of the most enlighten monarch that ever sit upon the russian throne determine to attempt a solution unfortunately on march 1 1881 the very day when alexander have give he approval to a scheme of constitutional reform involve the establishment of representative institution he be assassinate by revolutionary this fatal act put back the clock for twenty-five year the court and the nation be throw into the arm of the bureaucracy as they only protector against terrorism and reaction reign supreme meanwhile the bureaucracy grow more corrupt more tyrannical more inefficient every day while on the other hand the party of reform thrust as it be underground and hunt like rat become more and more bitter in spirit and more and more extreme in theory it be important to bear in mind that the struggle have never from begin to end be one which divide the nation as a whole into two hostile camp public opinion when it have not be indifferent have sway now to one side and now to the other accord as it be stir by some flagrant act of oppression on the part of the bureaucracy or some outrageous act of terrorism on the part of the revolutionary the truth be that the civil war in russium however a very real distinction between the _ intelligentsia _ and the peasant the _ intelligentsia _ be the few million educate russian who control or seek to control the destiny of the 145 million uneducated tiller of the soil there be nothing quite like they in this country though the expression the professional class describe they in part broadly speak they be people who have pass through policy the present war have raise in the mind of many man a question which we as a people will soon be call upon to answer be this war necessary or be it cause by the ambition and foolishness of statesman might it not have be avert if the people of europe have have more control over the way in which foreign policy be carry on out of these question have arise a demand for the democratisation of foreign policy that be for greater popular control over diplomatic negotiation in view of this it become necessary for every british citizen to gain some idea of what foreign policy be and by what principle it should be govern it be the purpose of this chapter to give first some account of the actual meaning of the word foreign policy and then secondly to consider how foreign policy may best be control in the interest of the whole population of the british empire and in the interest of the world at large a the meaning of foreign policy § 1 _ the foreign office _ -- to the ordinary man foreign policy be a affair of mystery and it not unnaturally rouse he suspicion he do not realize what be nevertheless the simple truth that he himself be both the material and the object of all foreign policy the business of the government of a country be to maintain and further the interest of the individual citizen that be the starting-point of all political institution the business of the foreign office be a part of this work of government and consist in the protection of the interest of the individual citizen where those interest depend upon the goodwill of a foreign government but just as in domestic politics the individual citizen be incline to suspect -- too often with truth -- that the government do not give impartial attention to the interest of all the citizen but be preoccupy in protect the interest of powerful and privileged person or group so in foreign policy the individual citizen be particularly prone to believe that the time of the foreign office be take up in further the interest of rich bondholder or powerful capitalist moreover the charge be sometimes hear that some of the most powerful of these capitalist be engage in the manufacture of armament and that the foreign office aim at secure order from foreign government for these firm thus encourage the nation of the world to provide themselves with means of destruction now just as no sensible man will say that government do not often oppress the people under they care so no sensible man will contend that foreign office do not sometimes sin in the same way but let we try to give a accurate picture of the work on which the british foreign office spend its time the organization of the foreign office consist of : -lrb- 1 -rrb- a office situate in down street man by a number of clerk under the direction of the secretary of state for foreign affair -lrb- 2 -rrb- the diplomatic service -- that be to say from three to eight official reside in the capital of each foreign country in the more important country these official be call a embassy and be under the direction of a ambassador in the smaller country they be call a legation and be under the direction of a minister these ambassador and minister receive instruction from and report to the secretary of state for foreign affair and be the mouthpiece of the british government in all business which great britain transact with foreign country -lrb- 3 -rrb- the consular service -- that be to say a large number of official call consul distribute over all the town of the world where british subject have important trade connection or where there be a considerable number of british subject these consul be under the direction of the foreign office and of the embassy or legation in the country where they reside and they business be to assist british trade and protect british subject § 2 _ the work of the foreign office _ -- the work of this whole organization may be divide into four class : -lrb- 1 -rrb- the protection of individual british subject this protection often extend to the most petty matter through the office of a consul and of a embassy or legation flow day by day a continual stream of british subject who be in small difficulty or have small grievance against the official of the country one old lady have lose she luggage a work man be strand without work and want to get back to england a commercial traveller have get into trouble with the custom official and ask for redress but the protection thus give be often concern with very important matter and be constantly employ on behalf of the poorest and the most helpless for instance we official in the united state be constantly occupy in assist british immigrant work man and woman who be suffer hardship under the stringent provision of the united state immigration law -lrb- 2 -rrb- the further of british trade it be the duty of the whole foreign office organization but especially of the consul to give advice to the representative of commercial firm to report opening for the sale of british goods abroad and generally to give assistance to british trade in its competition with foreign trade enquiry will for instance be receive by a consul at a chinese port from a manufacturer of pottery or harness or tin-tack ask what type of goods will be likely to find a market in that locality the consul will then enquire and give such information as he local knowledge enable he to supply or again a foreign country will sometimes make regulation which hinder the importation of english product english oats may for instance be affect with a blight which italy fear may infect she crop if she allow they importation it may then become the duty of the british embassy at rome to make arrangement with the italian government in order that english farmer may not suffer by lose the market for they produce but one important point must be remember because it be too often forget by those who criticise the foreign office there be one general restriction on the activity of the foreign office in assist british trade : no british official be allow to invite or try to persuade any foreign government to give order to british firm whether for war material or for any other article what we have already say apply to the relation between civilised country but the relation between civilised country on the one hand and uncivilised or semi-civilised country on the other hand be very much more difficult in many way difficulty especially arise with regard to commerce many of the less-developed country of the world such as some south american country and china can not like they richer neighbor undertake the development of they own resource they lack money scientific training business ability and so on they therefore give what be call concession to foreign company or capitalist that be the government of the country lease some industry for a term of year to the foreign company the mexican government for instance have lease its oil-well to english american and dutch company and the chinese government have largely confide the construction and management of its railroad to english french and german company now in many country where this happen the government be not strong enough or permanent enough to guarantee proper security of tenure to the foreign company to which it grant a concession very likely some official be bribe to grant the concession to one company and then bribe by another company to cancel it or the government be overthrow by a revolution and its successor cancel the concession it have grant by this mean british workman may be throw out of work and they employment may pass to workman in the united state or germany consequently foreign government -- the government of civilised country -- gradually begin to intervene and give protection to they subject who have concession in such country provide that they have obtain they concession in a respectable and proper manner competition between the different foreign company then grow up they government gradually begin to support they against each other in this competition until at last it become necessary for the different government if bad feeling be to be avoid to try to arrive at some arrangement among themselves fix the way in which the concession grant by this or that semi-civilised country shall be distribute among the subject of the great power something like this have be recently happen in china to a certain extent this line of action seem to be necessary in deal with backward country and it may be make mutually beneficial both to those country themselves and to the commerce of the great power but on the other hand the whole policy be obviously liable to great abuse consequently every self-respecting government know that all matter relate to concession must be treat with the greatest caution and forbearance and that the interest of all concern will be best serve in the long run by gradually help backward country along the path of civilisation and strengthen they government so that they may be able to assume complete control of they own finance and commercial enterprise we have now describe roughly the personal and the commercial work of the foreign office this work cover all the immediate interest of individual british citizen in regard to foreign country if each british subject be protect when abroad and if the trade and industry of the country on which the welfare and livelihood of every individual citizen ultimately depend be foster and safe-guarded then the primary duty of the british government in relation to other government have be discharge but this be not enough if the interest of the individual citizen of great britain be to be permanently secure in relation to foreign country we must be assure that the policy of foreign government be civilised and generally friendly to british subject there must be a general rule of law throughout the world on which british subject can count with assurance of safety and so the foreign office have a third and even more important class of work : -lrb- 3 -rrb- the maintenance of permanent good relation with foreign country these good relation be secure not only by continually friendly communication with foreign government over innumerable question of policy but also by the conclusion of a network of treaty some of they design to establish international co-operation in particular social or economic question such for instance as the exist treaty between great britain and france provide for the mutual payment of compensation under the workman 's compensation law of the two country and other conclude with the object of define the mutual policy of different country in general matter such as the regulation of trade the newest and most important class of treaty be those which like the hague convention and the treaty guarantee the neutrality of belgium and luxemburg attempt to lay down general rule of law which all country agree to observe in other word the office of diplomacy be to secure _ certainty _ in the government of the world so that every man may know what to expect in deal with he fellow-man of a different nationality it be difficult to describe adequately the complexity of this diplomatic work the economic and social system of the world have become so involve and intertwine that there be hardly anything one country can do which do not react in some way on the interest of the subject of another country in every european country and in the united state the government be be more and more call upon to regulate the delicate economic and social machinery on which modern life depend each government adopt a attitude towards such problem which be determine partly by the thought and the belief of its public man and partly by the course of historical development through which each country have pass there thus arise gradually in each country a more or less definite policy with which the country become identify formerly the policy of most european country be mainly confine to question arise in europe itself but in these day of industrial expansion the real aim of they policy generally lie outside europe there be vast region of the world where civilised government do not exist or be only begin to exist but where the citizen of civilised country travel and carry on trade no civilised country can prevent its trader go where they please -- indeed the prosperity of every great country now depend to some extent at least upon its trader find new market for the sale of they goods -- but if these trader go to a uncivilised country like central africa or the interior of china or the south sea island the civilised country not only feel oblige to protect they there but it must also by every claim of justice and humanity prevent they from ill-use the uncivilised and helpless native the horror which accompany the unregulated activity of foreign trader in a savage country may be see from the _ life of john g paton _ a missionary in the new hebride island of the southern pacific these island before they come under the government of any civilised power be visit by european and american trader especially trader in sandalwood the sandalwood trader write paton be as a class the most godless of man by they the poor defenceless native be oppress and rob on every hand and if they offer the slightest resistance they be ruthlessly silence by the musket or revolver the sale of intoxicant opium fire-arm and ammunition by the trader among the new hebridean have become a terrible and intolerable evil it become necessary for the civilised power to prohibit by international regulation the sale of fire-arm and intoxicant in the island such international regulation be always very difficult to enforce and finally the administration of the island be take over by great britain and france who now govern they jointly hence the civilised country of the world have gradually be lead to assume jurisdiction in uncivilised region and have convert many of they into colony or protectorate or sphere of influence by this process the interest of the nation of europe reach out into all the far corner of the earth and constant care and arrangement be need to prevent those interest clash where the interest of the different power do clash in a uncivilised or semi-civilised part of the world a general international agreement be often necessary to put thing straight for instance during recent year the interest of germany france and spain -- and to a less degree those of many other country -- be continually clash in morocco till it become necessary in 1906 to conclude a general international treaty call the algecira act whereby the relation of all the power with regard to morocco be define in great detail § 3 _ the balance of power _ -- it be this continual attempt to arrange matter and to keep the different power clear of each other in order that they interest may not clash which be the real underlie cause to-day of what be know as the balance of power the doctrine of the balance of power grow up at the end of the seventeenth and beginning of the eighteenth century when europe be threaten by the policy of aggression and conquest undertake by loui xiv of france from that day onward european statesman have seek to establish a definite european system and to limit the growth of the european state in such a way as to ensure that no state should be so strong as to threaten its neighbor the history of this attempt have be somewhat as follow a coalition of the state of europe be form against the aggression of loui xiv after a series of war a peace be sign at utrecht in 1713 define the boundary of the european state in such a way as to establish equality and a balance of power between they for about ten year european statesman attempt to maintain the system thus set up by means of what have since come to be know as the concert of europe -- that be by means of a series of international congress where opportunity be give for the settlement of dispute between the different state soon however it become impossible to satisfy the ambition of the ruler and people of europe by this mean and the concert of europe break up war follow during which those statesman especially in england who believe in the balance of power seek to prevent any european nation from be overwhelm by its enemy to this end england support austrium against the attack of prussium and then later support prussium against a coalition form by the rest of europe to crush she unfortunately neither england nor france have sufficient strength or courage to prevent the partition of poland between prussium russium and austrium which constitute a fatal violation of the balance of power peace do not return to europe till 1815 when the whole continent have be drive to combine for the overthrow of napoleon at the congress of vienna in that year the concert of europe be revive and for more than thirty year it practically succeed by means of a series of international congress in maintain a stable and balanced system in europe but this concert of europe be the very thing against which the democratic force on the continent finally rebel for the concert take the form of the so-called holy alliance between the ruler of europe whose object be to prevent popular movement from disturb the neat and orderly peace which they have create the system create by the congress of vienna begin to break down in 1848 since then the warlike nationalist and democratic movement in europe follow by the tremendous economic growth of the european nation have make it almost impossible to secure any stable balance of power though a more or less successful attempt to establish such a balance in the affair of south-eastern europe be make at the congress of berlin in 1878 the two hague conference of 1899 and 1907 do little but reveal the mutual fear and suspicion of the european nation though many statesman especially english and american labor sincerely to make the hague convention the guarantee of a lasting peace but it must be observe that the balance of power which be originally a distinctly european conception have now become a world-wide conception in order to secure a balance of power between the european state it be no longer sufficient to settle european frontier it be necessary to settle and as it be dovetail into each other the economic interest of the european country in africa asia and the southern pacific it be also necessary to define the relation of european country to the state in north and south america what be the conclusion to be draw from this history the idea of the balance of power be unsatisfactory you can not really balance live force nation be not dead mass which can be weigh against each other but live growth which expand accord to obscure natural law human law can never stop natural growth growth can only be stop by death and so the balance of power seem to necessitate continual conflict and so at least twice in the last two century the attempt to maintain a stable european system by a peaceful concert of europe have break down once in the holy alliance that concert itself become a intolerable tyranny many man to-day hope to secure peace by re-establish the concert of europe on a democratic basis but it may well be doubt whether any such system can be permanent unless there be a radical reform in the mind and character not only of european statesman but of the european people we shall discuss this later but meanwhile we may say this at least a balance of power be a imperfect conception it be a rough and ready -- almost barbarous -- policy the best that can be say for it be that no alternative policy have be devise or at least none have succeed every one of we who have a spark of idealism believe that the day will come when it shall give place to some more perfect system but at the present day not only international politics but also home politics be govern by this idea of a balance of power no democracy have yet be able to establish itself in any country except by virtue of a continual conflict between class and class between interest and interest between capital and labor and international conflict be but the reflection of the domestic conflict within each state both be continual unsuccessful attempt to reach a stable equilibrium and they can only be end by a true fusion of heart and will § 4 _ the estimation of national force _ -- it have be necessary to undertake this long discussion in order to give a more or less clear idea of the work do by diplomacy in maintain a stable international system arise out of this we have now to consider the fourth class of work -- and the most difficult -- which the foreign office have to perform for want of a better name we may call it -- -lrb- 4 -rrb- the estimation of national force nation be not mere agglomeration of individual they have each they own character they own feeling and they own life science have do little to determine the law of they growth but as we have see each nation do grow reach out slowly -- almost insensibly -- in this or that direction and gather to itself new interest which in they turn give new impulse to its growth perhaps the best simile that we can use for the foreign policy of the world be that of a rather tangle garden where creeper be continually grow and take root in new soil and where life be therefore always threatening and be threaten by new life the point be that we be deal with _ life _ -- with its growth and decay not with the movement of piece on a chequer-board now the foreign office largely exist in order to watch this growth and like a gardener to train and lead it in direction where it can expand without danger but for this work intimate knowledge be necessary -- knowledge not so much of the personal character or policy of those who govern the different nation but knowledge of the character the economic need the belief the feeling and the aspiration of the half-dumb million who form and ultimately determine the life of each nation the diplomatist must study every political and social movement which go on in a nation he must estimate the effect which the national system of education be have on the mind of the nation he must form a idea of the lesson which the government of he own country should learn from the government of other country whether it be for instance lesson in constitutional government or in municipal sanitation and he must above all be able to warn he government of the danger to he own country which the growth of foreign country seem to entail in order that peaceful measure may be take in time to prevent a collision this then be a rough account of the actual work of diplomacy it be not a full account there be many wrong thing do which deserve criticism but which we have not have space to mention there be also much self-sacrificing and thankless work do by diplomatist and consul in distant part of the world -- much seeming drudgery which can hope for no reward -- many honorable service render to the public of which the public never hear but the above account will suffice to give a rough idea of the organization with which we be deal and we may now pass on to consider the question of how this organization should be manage and control b the democratisation of foreign policy this phrase be rapidly become a political catchword as such it require to be approach with the utmost caution before go further it be necessary to test the assumption underlie it and to inquire how far they really correspond to the fact § 1 _ democracy and peace _ -- first of all the main assumption make by englishman who advocate the democratisation of foreign policy be that international peace would thereby be assure true the extension of the democratic principle be to many man a end in itself quite apart from the question whether it tend to peace but great mass of man be not move to make political demand merely by theoretical consideration it be the pressure of definite and imminent evil which arouse they to action in the case of england the demand for greater democratic control in the sphere of foreign policy arise in large measure from the sudden realisation in the late summer of 1911 at the time of the so-called agadir crisis that war between this country and germany be a possibility with which english statesman and the english people have to reckon we have feel the breath of war actually on we cheek and a large section of english sentiment revolt from it a demand be raise for a democratic policy of peace three year later on August 3 1914 when parliament meet to decide the happiness or suffering of the quarter of the human race comprise in the british empire the same demand be voice in a series of speech which accurately express the belief that peace be the policy of the people while war be the secret aim of they ruler mr t edmund harvey mp speak as follow : i be convince that this war for the great mass of the country of europe and not for we own country alone be no people 's war it be a war that have be make by man in high place by diplomatist work in secret by bureaucrat who be out of touch with the people of the world who be the remnant of a older evil civilisation which be disappear by gradual and peaceful method mr ponsonby mp speak in the same sense : i trust that even though it may be late the foreign secretary will use every endeavor to the very last moment disregard the tone of message and the manner of ambassador but look to the great central interest of humanity and civilisation to keep this country in a state of peace democracy mean peace -- can we accept this assumption contrast be sometimes illuminating and it may be well to turn from the parliamentary debate of August 3 to a article write sixty-two year ago in a english review by the greatest democrat of he time in April 1852 mazzinus publish in the _ westminster review _ a appeal to england to intervene on the continent in favor of the revolutionary movement in progress there since 1848 the following be a extract from that article : the menace of the foreigner weigh upon the smaller state the last spark of european liberty be extinguish under the dictatorial veto of the retrograde power england -- the country of elizabeth and cromwell -- have not a word to say in favor of the principle to which she owe she existence if england persist in maintain this neutral sword into the scale of european revolution -- it be a strange contrast which serve to remind we that the word democracy so lightly bandy about by political party have many different meaning and have stand for many different policy it may be roughly say that it stand for internationalism in 1792 when france claim as she mission the liberation of all nation under the tricolor it stand for call this more than a phase in the development of democratic doctrine it be a very difficult question which it would be presumptuous to try to answer offhand all we have try to show here be that on the whole the assumption as to the peaceful tendency of a democratic foreign policy be a doubtful one on which we must to some extent reserve we judgment § 2 _ foreign policy and popular force _ -- the above consideration will help we to appreciate at its true value the second main assumption which lie behind the demand for increase democratic control of foreign policy -- namely the assumption that the stuff of international politics be at present spin from the design of individual statesman and have no relation to the need of the people they govern state thus this idea will not bear examination for a moment the doctrine of the economic interpretation of history which have receive perhaps its most emphatic expression in the teaching of marxian socialist be now in one form or another accept by all think man but economics be after all a rough name for the sum of the ordinary need and effort of every single human being and the economic interpretation of history mean that the history of the world be in the long run determine by the cumulative force of these humble need and effort this and this alone be the real stuff of international politics statesman may attempt to find system but the only real force in international as in domestic politics be the education of the individual man 's desire it be indeed open to any critic to say that we present capitalist economic system be responsible for war because it dam up and divert from they true channel the need and the effort of the mass of mankind but to this a englishman may fairly answer that the free trade system under which we capitalist organization have reach its greatest development be build up by the manchester school with the sincere and avowed object of introduce universal peace cobden avowed this object clearly : i see he say in free trade that which shall act on the moral world as the law of gravitation in the universe draw man together thrust aside the antagonism of race and creed and language and unite we in the bond of eternal peace i believe that the desire and motive for large and mighty empire for gigantic army and mighty navy will die away yet in spite of these aspiration great war have come to england not once but at least three time since these word be speak and armament be immeasurably larger than ever before let we understand one thing clearly in connection with the present war mr ponsonby in the word already quote implored sir e gray to look to the great central interest of humanity and civilisation and to preserve the neutrality of england in those interest but at the moment at which he speak the eye of english statesman be look at one thing alone it be not a question of what french statesman expect they to do the british government have explain quite clearly to french statesman that they must not expect armed support from england this fact have be make clear to the french foreign office long before in a series of conversation between the statesman issue _ -- the war of 1914 be not simply a war between the dual alliance and the triple entente : it be for great britain and germany especially a war of idea -- a conflict between two different and irreconcilable conception of government society and progress a attempt will be make in this chapter to make clear what these conception be and to discuss the issue between they as impartially as possible from the point of view not of either of the combatant power but of human civilisation as a whole there be really two great controversy be fight out between great britain and germany : one about the end of national policy and another about the means to be adopt towards those or any other end the latter be the issue raise by the german chancellor 's plea -- not so unfamiliar on the lip of we own countryman as we be now tempt to believe -- that necessity know no law it be the issue of law and scrap of paper against force against what some apologist have call the philosophy of advance by organised terrorism and devastation be the public enemy of the civilised world but it be a remarkable and significant fact that the policy in which this ruthless theory be embody command question of belgian neutrality and the event which precipitate the british ultimatum what we know to be a false version of the fact be current in germany as be evident from the publish statement of the leader of german thought and opinion and it may be many year before its currency be displaced this difficulty should serve to remind we how defective the machinery of civilisation still be one of more to enforce its decision on the question at issue between the european power it have not even the machinery for ascertain the fact of the case and bring they to the notice of neutral government and people in the name of civilisation as a whole but apart from divergent belief as to the fact it be remarkable that think germany should be in sympathy with the spirit and tone of german policy
