7 _ the future of civilisation _ -- what hope dare we cherish in this hour of conflict for the future of civilisation the great the supreme task of human politics and statesmanship be to extend the sphere of law let other labor to make man culture or virtuous or happy these be the task of the teacher the priest and the common man the statesman 's task be simpler it be to enfold they in a jurisdiction which will enable they to live the life of they soul ' choice the state say the greek philosopher be the foundation of the good life but its crown rise far above mere citizenship there where the state end cry nietzsche -lrb- 1 -rrb- echo aristotle and the great tradition of civilised political thought there _ man begin _ there where the state end look thither my brother do you not see the rainbow and the bridge to the overman ever since organise society begin the standard of the individual the ideal of priest and teacher the doctrine of religion and morality have outstrip the practice of statesmanship for the polestar of the statesman have not be love but law he not the task of exhort man to love one another but the simpler duty of enforce the law thou shalt not kill and in that simple strenuous necessary task statesman and political thinker have watch the slow extension of the power of law from the family to the tribe from the tribe to the city from the city to the nation from the nation to the commonwealth when will law take its next extension when will warfare which be murder between individual and rebellion between group of citizen be equally preventable between nation by the common law of the world -lrb- footnote 1 : _ also sprach zarathustra _ speech xi -lrb- end -rrb- -rrb- the answer be simple when the world have a common will and have create a common government to express and enforce that will in the sphere of science and invention of industry and economics as norman angell and other have teach we the world be already one great society for the merchant the banker and the stockbroker political frontier have be break down trade and industry respond to the reaction of a single world-wide nervous system shock and panic pass as freely as airman over border and custom-house and not big business only but the humblest citizen in he search for a livelihood find himself catch in the mesh of the same world-wide network the widow who take in wash say graham walla -lrb- 1 -rrb- in he deep and search analysis of we contemporary life fail or succeed accord to she skill in choose starch or soda or a wring machine under the influence of half a dozen compete world-scheme of advertisement the english factory girl who be urge to join she union the tired old scotch gatekeeper with a few pound to invest the galician peasant when the emigration agent call the artisan in a french provincial town whose industry be threaten by a new invention all know that unless they find they way among world-wide fact which only reach they through mislead word they will be crush the industrial revolution of the past century steam-power and electricity the railway and the telegraph have knit mankind together and make the world one place -lrb- footnote 1 : _ the great society _ -lrb- 1914 -rrb- p 4 -rrb- but this new great society be as yet formless and inarticulate it be not only devoid of common leadership and a common government it lack even the beginning of a common will a common emotion and a common consciousness of the great society consciously or unconsciously we must all perforce be member but of the great state the great world-commonwealth we do not yet discern the rudiment the economic organization of the world have outstrip the development of its citizenship and government : the economic man with he farsighted vision and scientific control of the resource of the world must sit by and see the work of he hand lay in ash by contend government and people no man can say how many generation must pass before the platitude of the market and the exchange pass into the current language of politics § 8 _ the two road of advance : inter-state action and common citizenship _ -- in the great work which lie before the statesman and people of the world for the extension of law and common citizenship and the prevention of war there be two parallel line of advance one road lie through the development of what be know as international but should more properly be call _ inter-state law _ through the revival on a firmer and broader foundation of the concert of europe conceive by the congress of vienna just a hundred year ago -- itself a revival on a secular basis of the great mediaeval ideal of a international christendom hold together by christian law and christian ideal that ideal fade away for ever at the reformation which group europe into independent sovereign state rule by man responsible to no one outside they own border it will never be revive on a ecclesiastical basis can we hope for its revival on a basis of modern democracy modern nationality and modern educate public opinion can inter-state law hitherto a mere shadow of the majestic name it bear almost a matter of convention and etiquette with no permanent tribunal to interpret it and no government to enforce it be enthrone with the necessary power to maintain justice between the people and government of the world such a law the statesman of great britain and russium seek to impose on europe in 1815 to maintain a state of affair which history have show to have be intolerable to the european people there be those who hope that the task can be resume on a better basis at the next congress shall we try again write professor gilbert murray -lrb- 1 -rrb- to achieve castlereagh 's and alexander 's ideal of a permanent concert pledge to make collective war upon the peace-breaker surely we must we must at all cost and in spite of all difficulty because the alternative means such unspeakable failure we must learn to agree we civilised nation of europe or else we must perish i believe that the chief council of wisdom here be to be sure to go far enough we need a permanent concert perhaps a permanent common council in which every awkward problem can be deal with before it have time to grow dangerous and in which outvote minority must accustom themselves to give way -lrb- footnote 1 : _ hibbert journal _ oct 1914 p 77 -rrb- other utterance by public man such as mr roosevelt and we own prime minister might be cite in the same sense but professor murray 's have be choose because he have have the courage to grasp the nettle in he word the true position be quite clearly set forth if inter-state law be to become a reality we must be sure to go far enough there be no half-way house between law and no law between government and no government between responsibility and no responsibility if the new concert be to be effective it must be able to compel the submission of all awkward problem and cause of quarrel to its permanent tribunal at the hague or elsewhere and it must be able to enforce the decision of its tribunal employ for the purpose if necessary the armed force of the signatory power as a international police out-vote minority must accustom themselves to give way it be a bland and easy phrase but it involve the whole question of world-government man must accustom themselves not to demand a eye for a eye and a tooth for a tooth the earliest law-giver might have say when the state first intervene between individual to make itself responsible for public order peace between the power as between individual be no doubt a habit to which cantankerous power must accustom themselves but they will be sure to do so if there be a law arm with the force to be they schoolmaster towards peaceable habit in other word they will do so because they have surrender one of the most vital element in the independent life of a state -- the right of conduct its own policy -- to the jurisdiction of a higher power a inter-state concert with a judiciary of its own and a army and navy under its own order be in fact not a inter-state concert at all it be a new state : it be in fact the world-state there be no middle course between law and no law : and the essence of statehood as we have see be a common law will this new state have the other attribute of government -- a common legislature and a common executive -- as well as a common judiciary let we go back to professor murray 's word he speak of outvote minority let we suppose the refractory country to be great britain outvote on some question relate to sea-power of whom will the outvote minority consist of the british member on the common council of the concert but the question at once arise what be the credentials of these british member whom do they represent to whom be they responsible if they be the representative of the british people and responsible to the democracy which send they how can they be expect to accustom themselves to give way -- perhaps to a majority compose of the representative of undemocratic government they responsibility be not to the concert but to they own government and people they be not the minority member of a democratically-elected council of they own fellow-citizen they be the minority member of a heterogeneous council towards which they owe no allegiance and recognize no binding responsibility there be no half-way house between citizenship and no citizenship between responsibility and no responsibility no man and no community can serve two master when the point of conflict arise man and nation have to make the choice where they duty lie not the representative of great britain on the international concert but the people of great britain themselves would have to decide whether they real allegiance as citizen be due to the world-state or to they own commonwealth : they would find themselves at the same awful parting of the way which confront the people of the southern state in 1861 when at the outbreak of the civil war general lee be offer by lincoln the commandership of the northern army and refuse it to become the commander-in-chief on the side of the south he do so because he believe as he tell congress after the war that the act of virginium in withdraw herself from the united state carry he along with it as a citizen of virginium and that _ she _ law and act be bind on he in other word unless the propose common council be to be make something more than a council of the delegate of sovereign state -lrb- as the southern state believe themselves to be till 1861 -rrb- a deadlock sooner or later be almost inevitable and the terrible and difficult question -- so familiar to american and recently to ourselves on the smaller stage of ulster -- of the right of secession and the coercion of minority will arise but if the common council be frame in accordance with a constitution which bind its representative to accept its decision and obey its government then the world-state with a world-executive will already have come into be there will be no more war but only rebellion and treason such be the real meaning of proposal to give a binding sanction to the decision of a inter-state concert anything short of this -- treaty and arbitration-agreement base upon inter-state arrangement without any executive to enforce they -- may give relief for a time and pave the way for further progress but can in itself provide no permanent security no satisfactory justification for the neglect of defensive measure by the various sovereign government on behalf of they people mr bryan for the united state have within the last eighteen month conclude twenty-six general arbitration treaty with different government and may yet succeed in he ambition of sign treaty with all the remainder yet no one imagine that when the immunity of the united state from attack be guarantee by the promise of every government in the world america will rely for she defense upon those promise alone in discuss proposal for a european council then we must be quite sure to face all that it mean but let we not reject professor murray 's suggestion off-hand because of its inherent difficulty : for that man should be discuss such scheme at all mark a significant advance in we political thought only let we be quite clear as to what they presuppose they presuppose the supremacy in the collective mind of civilised mankind of law over force a definite supremacy of what may be call the civilian as against the military ideal not in a majority of state but in every state powerful enough to defy coercion they presuppose a world map definitely settle on line satisfactory to the national aspiration of the people they presuppose a _ status quo _ which be not simply maintain like that after 1815 because it be a legal fact and its disturbance would be inconvenient to the exist ruler but because it be inherently equitable -lrb- 1 -rrb- they presuppose a similar democratic basis of citizenship and representation among the component state they presuppose lastly a educate public opinion incomparably less selfish less ignorant less unsteady less materialistic and less narrowly national than have be prevalent hitherto let we work and hope for these thing : let we use we best effort to remove misunderstanding and promote a sense of common responsibility and common trusteeship for civilisation between the people of all the various sovereign state but meanwhile let we work also with better hope of immediate if less ambitious success along the other parallel road of advance -lrb- footnote 1 : the same apply to proposal for ensure permanent peace in the industrial sphere neither capital nor labor will abide by scrap of paper if they do not feel the _ status quo -lrb- ie _ the condition under which wage-contract be make -rrb- to be equitable and inherently just -rrb- the other road may seem in this hour of dream and disaster of extreme of hope and disillusionment a long and tedious track : it be the old slow high road of civilisation not the short cut across the field it look forward to abide result not through the mechanical co-operation of government but through the growth of a organic citizenship through the education of the nation themselves to a sense of common duty and a common life it look forward not to the definite establishment in we day of the world-state but only to the definite refutation of the wicked theory of the mutual incompatibility of nation it look forward to the expression in the outward order of the world 's government of what we may call the principle of the commonwealth of lord acton 's great principle of the state compose of free nation of the state as a living body which live through the organic union and free activity of its several national member and it find its immediate field of action in the deepen and extension of the obligation of citizenship among the people of the great free just peace-loving supra-national commonwealth whose patriotism have be build up not by precept and doctrine but on a firm foundation of older loyalty the principle of the commonwealth be not a european principle : it be a world-principle it do not proceed upon the expectation of a united state of europe for all the great power of europe except austria-hungary -lrb- and some of the smaller such as holland belgium and portugal -rrb- be extra-european power also indeed if we contract we view with gladstone and bismarck and the statesman of the last generation to european issue alone we shall be ignore the chief political problem of we age -- the contact of race and nation with wide variety of social experience and at different level of civilisation it be this great and insistent problem -lrb- call it the problem of east and west or the problem of the colour-line -rrb- in all its difficult ramification political social and above all economic which make the development of the principle of the commonwealth the most pressing political need of we age for the problem arise out of the contact of race and nation can never be adjust either by the wise action of individual or by conflict and warfare they can only be solve by fair and deliberate statesmanship within the bosom of a single state through the recognition by both party of a higher claim than they own sectional interest -- the claim of a common citizenship and the interest of civilisation -lrb- 1 -rrb- it be here in the union and collaboration of diverse race and people that the principle of the commonwealth find its peculiar field of operation without this principle and without its expression however imperfect in the british empire the world would be in chaos to-day -lrb- footnote 1 : the most recent example of this be the settlement of the very difficult dispute between indium and south africa -rrb- we can not predict the political development of the various great power who between they control the destiny of civilisation we can not estimate the degree or the manner in which france free at last from nearer preoccupation will seek to embody in she vast dominion the great civilising principle for which she republic stand we can not foretell the issue of the conflict of idea which have sway to and fro in russium between the british and the prussian method of deal with the problem of nationality germany italy japan -- here too we be face by enigma one other great commonwealth remain besides the british upon the united state already lie the responsibility voluntarily assume and except during a time of internal crisis -lrb- 1 -rrb- successfully discharge of secure peace from external foe for score of million of inhabitant of the american continent yet with the progress of event she responsibility must yearly enlarge : for both the immigrant nationality within and the world-problem without she border seem to summon she to a deeper education and to wider obligation -lrb- footnote 1 : french occupation of mexico 1862 during the american civil war when the monroe doctrine be temporarily in abeyance -rrb- but upon the vast ramify and inchoate commonwealth of great britain lie the heaviest responsibility it be a task unequally share between those of she citizen who be capable of discharge it she task within the commonwealth be to maintain the common character and ideal and to adjust the mutual relation of one quarter of the human race she task without be to throw she weight into the scale of peace and to uphold and develop the standard and validity of inter-state agreement it be a task which require even at this time of crisis when by the common sentiment of she citizen the real nature and purpose of the commonwealth have become clear to we the active thought of all political student for to bring home to all within she border who bear rule and responsibility from the village headman in indium and nigeria the basutu chief and the south sea potentate to the public opinion of great britain and the self-governing dominion the nature of the british commonwealth and the character of its citizenship and ideal and to study how those ideal may be better express in its working institution and executive government -- that be a task to which the present crisis beckon the mind of british citizen a task which britain owe not only to herself but to mankind _ note _ -- a friendly critic who see this chapter in m remark : i think the author have be very successful in ignore some of the shady method by which the british empire
